      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5322068-kl-cat?shelf=haven-t-i-already-read-something-si">haven-t-i-already-read-something-si</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5322068-kl-cat?shelf=what-is-this-shit">what-is-this-shit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5322068-kl-cat?shelf=die-just-die">die-just-die</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5322068-kl-cat?shelf=death-by-hype-train">death-by-hype-train</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5322068-kl-cat?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1077514128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12852368240421925036">I shall never ever touch this book in my life, and will advice my school librarian to do so as well. (The single star is simply for shit and giggles)<br/><br/><a href='http://bibliodaze.com/2014/10/on-wanting-a-book-to-fail/' rel='nofollow noopener'>For those who may ask why.</a><br/><br/><b>Edit:</b><br/><br/>Haha, a few disgruntled trolls decided to message me on how I can't judge a novel from where it's published. Screw that. So I decided to take initiative and read the first chapter and good grief, my eyes. I swear that my Harry Potter fan fiction has better writing that this.<br/><blockquote>"Marcus Loxias Megalos is bored. He cannot re</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12852368240421925036" style="display:none">I shall never ever touch this book in my life, and will advice my school librarian to do so as well. (The single star is simply for shit and giggles)<br /><br /><a href="http://bibliodaze.com/2014/10/on-wanting-a-book-to-fail/" rel="nofollow noopener">For those who may ask why.</a><br /><br /><b>Edit:</b><br /><br />Haha, a few disgruntled trolls decided to message me on how I can't judge a novel from where it's published. Screw that. So I decided to take initiative and read the first chapter and good grief, my eyes. I swear that my Harry Potter fan fiction has better writing that this.<br /><blockquote>"Marcus Loxias Megalos is bored. He cannot remember a time before the boredom. School is boring. Girls are boring. Football is boring."</blockquote>See here, ladies and gentlemen of the jury. This is the opening sentence of the novel. Note the spectacular eloquence as the coauthors convey Marcus' feelings. Such marvellous writing; compared, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/338705.Catherynne_M__Valente" title="Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherynne M. Valente</a> has plenty to catch up on terms of prose. <blockquote>"Marcus wears baggy black gym shorts and is shirtless. His 24 ribs show through his tanned skin. His arms are sinewy and hard. His breathing is easy. His stomach is taut and his hair is close-cropped and black and his eyes are green. A bead of sweat rolls down the tip of his nose. All of Istanbul simmers on this night, and Marcus is no different."</blockquote>Ooh, is that what I think it is? Why, I must be mistaken! Surely the authors couldn't have conformed to using the pseudo-literary device of going against "show, don't tell" at such an early stage of the chapter, let alone novel? (This is the third paragraph.) Well, I suppose showing is a technique rarely employed by brilliant writers nowadays, or heaven forbid, expected. I must have words with my 7th grade English teacher.<br /><blockquote>“But immediately afterward in terror and confusion—deep, true, and profound terror and confusion”</blockquote> Clever of the authors to correctly guess I didn't catch 'terror and confusion' the first time. <blockquote>"Unlike Odysseus, war will never find Marcus. There will be no grand journey.... He holds a 9,000-year-old knife, made of a single piece of bronze forged in the fires of Knossos..."</blockquote>Grand allusions to Greek mythology! How terribly well-read the authors must be, as they reveal their exemplary knowledge to us, the mere <s>mortals</s> readers. I am basking in the glow of higher enlightenment. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ “For once, the legends have become a beautiful reality.” Okay, fuck you so hard, James Frey of the literary fiction sweatshops. How <i>dare</i> you compare the goddamn epic of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1375.The_Iliad_The_Odyssey" title="The Iliad/The Odyssey by Homer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iliad/The Odyssey</a> to the plot of your shitty rip off from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8894139.The_39_Clues_Set__Books_1___7_" title="The 39 Clues Set (Books 1 - 7) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The 39 Clues Set</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>. With inexplicably, aliens. <u>The Odyssey</u> is about base human emotions, not heroic ideals. Odysseus of metis is beautifully complex. He is most definitely not a pathetic boy that lies around watching television, poorly written as a cardboard caricature attempted to represent "the villain" archetype. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><blockquote>"He has slept with it under his pillow since he was six. He has killed chickens, rats, dogs, cats, pigs, horses, hawks, and lambs with it. He has killed 11 people with it. He is 16, in his prime for Playing." </blockquote> Lists, I'm sure as you know, are proofs of flawless prose. Why, I can just <i>feel</i> the angst and terribly deep anger inside Marcus. I'm sure that he'll make <i>the</i> ultimate love interest for those female heroines in YA supernatural novels. <br /><br />Yep, and that's chapter one. Reading anymore would most likely result in either tossing myself out of the window or the novel itself. Because, you know, it's just so so terribly good and I am unworthy of reading another chapter, let alone having the novel within a one mile radius. How awfully sad that would be. <br /><br />God. It seems my storage of sarcasm has ran out for the day. *goes off to write fan fiction*<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12852368240421925036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_17179933'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17179933-das-labyrinth-erwacht"><img alt="Das Labyrinth erwacht (Labyrinth #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1356436946l/17179933._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('U1p2vhlItn61EGbzhrE0vRfcBjMjvWZSAoD2Eh5KOhczYlNeIhnjw+2D1KX7bOP0HaRdU47gq8i/4yVa7DUStw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Hr7DyWJcbLqKAl9aoTQ9qxRC+me89ppaPexVNlJw+SN+huYpWQ05B9KR7Qzc6eriHjqhBxGrV8CAj4Z+oA/Rgw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13242458295089089831">James Christopher Frey is an American author and entrepreneur. After battling with alcohol addiction and spending time in rehab, he wrote <i>A Million Little Pieces</i> which was published in 2003 in America and the following year in the UK to critical acclaim. He wrote the sequel, <i>My Friend Leonard</i> about life after rehab, which was published in 2005 in the US and the year after in the UK.<br/><br/>James Frey now </span>
  <span id="freeText13242458295089089831" style="display:none">James Christopher Frey is an American author and entrepreneur. After battling with alcohol addiction and spending time in rehab, he wrote <i>A Million Little Pieces</i> which was published in 2003 in America and the following year in the UK to critical acclaim. He wrote the sequel, <i>My Friend Leonard</i> about life after rehab, which was published in 2005 in the US and the year after in the UK.<br /><br />James Frey now lives in New York with his wife, daughter and dog. He is still writing. Most recently he has published Bright Shiny Morning, and his new book The Final Testament of the Holy Bible will publish on 12 April and is available for pre-order now.<br /><br />He is also one of the authors that share the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3380908.Pittacus_Lore" title="Pittacus Lore" rel="nofollow noopener">Pittacus Lore</a>, author of the Lorien Legacies.<br /><br />Books coming out of James Frey's YA book packaging company Full Fathom Five: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/list/show/45872.Full_Fathom_Five#18053060">https://www.goodreads.com/list/show/4...</a></span>
